<P align="left"><B>NOTE&nbsp;1&nbsp;&#151; BASIS OF PRESENTATION</B>

<P align="left">
The accompanying unaudited condensed consolidated financial
statements of Dell Computer Corporation (the &#147;Company&#148;)
 should be read in conjunction with the consolidated financial
statements and notes thereto filed with the U.S.&nbsp;Securities
and Exchange Commission in the Company&#146;s Annual Report on
Form&nbsp;10-K for the fiscal year ended January&nbsp;28, 2000.
In the opinion of management, the accompanying condensed
consolidated financial statements reflect all adjustments of a
normal recurring nature considered necessary to present fairly
the financial position of the Company and its consolidated
subsidiaries at July&nbsp;28, 2000 and January&nbsp;28, 2000 and
the results of their operations and their cash flows for the
three and six month periods ended July&nbsp;28, 2000 and
July&nbsp;30, 1999. Certain prior period amounts have been
reclassified to conform to the current period presentation.

<P align="left"><B>NOTE&nbsp;3&nbsp;&#151; EARNINGS PER COMMON SHARE</B>

<P align="left">
Basic earnings per share is based on the weighted effect of all
common shares issued and outstanding and is calculated by
dividing net income by the weighted average shares outstanding
during the period. Diluted earnings per share is calculated by
dividing net income by the weighted average number of common
shares used in the basic earnings per share calculation plus the
number of common shares that would be issued assuming conversion
of all potentially dilutive common shares outstanding. The
following table sets forth the computation of basic and diluted
earnings per share (in millions, except per share amounts):

<P align="left"><B>NOTE&nbsp;4&nbsp;&#151; COMPREHENSIVE INCOME</B>

<P align="left">
The Company&#146;s comprehensive income is comprised of net
income, foreign currency translation adjustments and unrealized
gains and losses on marketable securities held as
available-for-sale investments. Comprehensive income was
$973&nbsp;million and $522&nbsp;million for the three-month
periods ended July&nbsp;28, 2000 and July&nbsp;30, 1999,
respectively, and $1,403&nbsp;million and $970&nbsp;million for
the six-month periods ended July&nbsp;28, 2000 and July&nbsp;30,
1999, respectively.

<P align="center">4

<H5 align="left"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<P align="left"><B>NOTE&nbsp;5&nbsp;&#151; RECENTLY ISSUED ACCOUNTING
PRONOUNCEMENT</B>

<P align="left">
In December 1999, the Securities and Exchange Commission released
 Staff Accounting Bulletin No.&nbsp;101, Revenue Recognition in
Financial Statements (&#147;SAB&nbsp;101&#148;), providing the
SEC&#146;s view with respect to the application of generally
accepted accounting principles to selected revenue recognition
issues. As amended, SAB&nbsp;101 will become effective for the
fourth quarter of fiscal 2001. The Company is currently assessing
 the impact of SAB&nbsp;101 and currently believes that the
effect, if any, will not have a material effect on the
Company&#146;s financial position or overall trends in results of
 operations.

<P align="left"><B>NOTE&nbsp;6&nbsp;&#151; SEGMENT INFORMATION</B>

<P align="left">
The Company has three reportable business segments: the Americas,
 Europe and Asia-Pacific and Japan regions.

<P align="left">
The accounting policies of the geographic segments are the same
as those described in the summary of significant accounting
policies in the Company&#146;s Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K
for the fiscal year ended January&nbsp;28, 2000. The Company
allocates resources to and evaluates performance of its
geographic segments based on balanced priorities of liquidity,
profitability and growth. Transfers between geographic areas are
recorded using internal transfer prices set by the Company.

reportable segments for the three and six month periods ended

arising in the ordinary course of business. The Company&#146;s
management does not expect that the outcome in any of these legal
 proceedings, individually or collectively, will have a material
adverse effect on the Company&#146;s financial condition, results
 of operations or cash flows.

<P align="left"><I>Net Revenue</I>

<P align="left">
During the second quarter of fiscal 2001, the Company generated
record performance in terms of net revenues, unit sales, net
income and earnings per share. Consolidated net revenue increased
 25% and 28% in the second quarter and first six months of fiscal
 2001, respectively, over the comparable periods of fiscal 2000,
and increased 5% over the first quarter of fiscal 2001. The
increase in consolidated net revenue was primarily attributable
to increased units sold. Unit sales increased 22% and 26% in the
second quarter and first six months of fiscal year 2001,
respectively, as compared to the same periods of fiscal 2000.

<P align="left">
In the Americas region, net revenue grew 27% in the second
quarter of fiscal 2001 compared to the same quarter of fiscal
2000. Net revenue in the Europe region increased 10% during the
second quarter of fiscal 2001 compared to the same period of the
prior fiscal year, and Asia-Pacific and Japan net revenue
increased 48% during the second quarter of fiscal 2001 compared
to the same period of the prior fiscal year.

<P align="left">
Average revenue per unit sold increased 2% for the second fiscal
quarter of 2001 compared to the prior year and decreased 2% on a
sequential basis, primarily resulting from the Company&#146;s
efforts to balance competitive pricing with a focus on increased
profitability, while operating in an environment of variable
component pricing and availability.

<P align="left">
Unit sales increased across all product lines for the second
quarter and first six months of fiscal 2001 over the comparable
periods of fiscal 2000. Supplementing its already strong
traditional desktop PC business, the Company continues to
generate more of its unit sales mix from high-end products at
both the core and the edge of the Internet Infrastructure
build-out. The Company&#146;s enterprise systems, including
servers, workstations and storage products, address needs at the
core of the Internet Infrastructure, where companies are
installing robust server and storage systems that power online
commerce and store information for retrieval. Enterprise systems
sales grew 46% during the second quarter of fiscal 2001 compared
to the second quarter of fiscal 2000, and 8% on a sequential
basis. At the edge of the Internet Infrastructure, users are
buying a variety of devices to access and leverage the core. The
Company&#146;s notebook computers address the mobile computing
needs of users, and its desktop computers continue to represent
an important part of the Company&#146;s product offerings. During
 the second quarter of fiscal 2000, notebook computer unit sales
increased 60% compared to the same period for fiscal 2000, and 8%
 on a sequential basis. Desktop computer unit sales increased 7%
compared to the prior year period, and increased 1% sequentially.
 During the second quarter of fiscal 2001,

<P align="center">7

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left"><A HREF="#toc">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV align="left">
enterprise systems comprised 19% of system revenue, compared with
 16% during the second quarter of fiscal 2000; notebook computers
 comprised 30% of system revenue, compared with 24% during the
same period of the prior fiscal year; and desktop computers
comprised 51% of system revenues, compared with 60% during the
same period in fiscal 2000.
</DIV>

<P align="left">
Additionally, as the Internet continues to pull a number of
products and services into an online environment, the Company has
 begun to broaden its revenue base beyond the core system,
commonly referred to as &#147;beyond the box&#148; revenues.
These offerings, which include warranty services, product
integration and installation services, Internet access,
web-hosting services, DellWare, Gigabuys, peripherals, technology
 consulting and other offerings, enhance the Company&#146;s core
system offerings. Beyond the box revenues comprised approximately
 17% and 16% of net revenues during the second quarter of fiscal
2001 and 2000, respectively.

<P align="left"><I>Gross Margin</I>

<P align="left">
As a percentage of consolidated net revenue, gross margin
increased on a sequential basis from 20.5% in the first quarter
of fiscal 2001 to 21.3% in the second quarter of fiscal 2001. As
compared to the second quarter of fiscal 2000, gross margin
decreased from 22.0%. On a year to date basis, gross margin
decreased from 21.8% during the first six months of fiscal 2000
to 20.9% during the first six months of fiscal 2001. The
relatively stable margins are primarily the result of the
factors, referred to above, affecting average revenue per unit.

<P align="left"><I>Operating Expenses</I>

<P align="left">
Selling, general and administrative expenses increased in
absolute dollar amounts for the second quarter and first half of
fiscal 2001 and increased as a percentage of consolidated net
revenue from the same periods in fiscal 2000. The increase in
absolute dollars was due primarily to the Company&#146;s increase
 in staffing and increased infrastructure expenses, including
information systems, to support the Company&#146;s continued
growth.

<P align="left">
The Company continues to invest in research, development and
engineering activities to develop and introduce new products and
to support its continued goal of improving and developing
efficient procurement, manufacturing and distribution processes.
As a result, research, development and engineering expenses have
increased each year in absolute dollars due to increased staffing
 levels and product development costs, although, as a percent of
revenue, these costs have remained level. The Company expects to
continue to increase its research, development and engineering
spending in absolute dollar amounts.

<P align="left">
The Company believes that its ability to manage operating
expenses is an important factor in its ability to remain
competitive and successful. The Company will continue to invest
in personnel, information systems and other infrastructure, as
well as in research, development and engineering activities to
support its continued growth and to continue to develop new,
competitive products and more efficient methods of delivery. It
is the Company&#146;s goal to manage operating expenses, over
time, relative to its net revenue and gross margin.

<P align="left"><I>Income Taxes</I>

<P align="left">
The Company&#146;s effective tax rate was approximately 30% for
the second quarter and first six months of fiscal 2001 and fiscal
 2000.

<P align="left">
During the first six months of fiscal 2001, the Company generated
 approximately $2&nbsp;billion in cash flows from operating
activities, which represents the Company&#146;s principal source
of cash. Cash flows from operating activities resulted primarily
from the Company&#146;s net income, adjusted for income tax
benefits resulting from the exercise of employee stock options,
and changes in operating working capital.

<P align="left">
At July&nbsp;28, 2000, the Company had approximately
$8.3&nbsp;billion of cash and investments. Of that amount,
strategic investments totaled approximately $2.2&nbsp;billion, an
 increase in total value of approximately $707&nbsp;million
compared to January&nbsp;28, 2000. The increase in value was due
to additional investments and net appreciation, and was partially
 offset by sales of equity securities. Of the total value at
July&nbsp;28, 2000, approximately $1.3&nbsp;billion represented
unrealized appreciation. The Company expects to continue to make
strategic investments in order to enhance and extend the
company&#146;s strategic initiatives.

<P align="left">
As compared to the second quarter of fiscal 2000, both days of
sales in accounts receivable and days in accounts payable
decreased by one day, whereas days of supply in inventory
increased by one day. The company&#146;s cash conversion cycle
changed to a negative 14&nbsp;days in the second quarter of
fiscal 2001 from a negative 15&nbsp;days in the second quarter of
 fiscal 2000. The Company&#146;s return on invested capital, a
key indicator of efficient asset management, increased to 294%
for the second quarter of fiscal year 2001, from 292% for the
first quarter of fiscal 2001, and from 260% for the second
quarter of the prior year.

<P align="left">
During the second quarter of fiscal 2001, the Company repurchased
 11.9&nbsp;million shares of common stock for an aggregate cost
of $521&nbsp;million, primarily to manage the dilution resulting
from shares issued under the Company&#146;s employee stock plans.
 By the end of the quarter, the Company had repurchased
829&nbsp;million shares out of its authorized 1&nbsp;billion
share repurchase program. At July&nbsp;28, 2000, the Company held
 equity options and forwards that allow for the purchase of
90&nbsp;million shares of common stock at various times through
the first quarter of fiscal 2004, at an average price of
$51&nbsp;per share. At July&nbsp;28, 2000, the Company also had
outstanding put obligations covering 107&nbsp;million shares with
 an average exercise price of $46&nbsp;per share. The Company
anticipates that it will continue to use excess liquidity to
repurchase common stock.

<P align="left">
The Company utilized $236&nbsp;million in cash during the first
six months of fiscal 2001 to improve and equip its manufacturing
and office facilities as the Company continues to grow. Cash
flows for similar capital expenditures for the full fiscal year
are expected to total approximately $500&nbsp;million.

<P align="left">
The Company maintains master lease facilities providing the
capacity to fund up to $1.3&nbsp;billion. The combined facilities
 provide for the ability of the Company to lease certain real
property, buildings and equipment to be constructed or acquired.
At July&nbsp;28, 2000, $458&nbsp;million of the combined
facilities had been utilized.

<P align="left">
Management believes that the Company has sufficient resources
from cash provided from operations and available borrowings to
support its operations and capital requirements for at least the
next 12&nbsp;months.

<P align="left"><B>Factors Affecting the Company&#146;s Business and Prospects
</B>

<P align="left">
There are numerous factors that affect the Company&#146;s
business and the results of its operations. These factors include
 general economic and business conditions; the level of demand
for the Company&#146;s products and services; the level and
intensity of competition in the computer industry and the pricing
 pressures that may result; the ability of the Company to timely
and effectively manage periodic product transitions, as well as
component availability and cost; the ability of the Company to
develop new products based on new or evolving technology and the
market&#146;s acceptance of those products; the ability of the
Company to manage its inventory levels to minimize excess
inventory, declining inventory values and obsolescence; the
product, customer and geographic sales mix of any particular
period; and the Company&#146;s ability to continue to improve its
 infrastructure (including personnel and systems) to keep pace
with the growth in its overall business activities. For a
discussion of these and other factors affecting the
Company&#146;s business and prospects, see
&#147;Item&nbsp;1&nbsp;&#151; Business&nbsp;&#151; Factors
Affecting the Company&#146;s Business and Prospects&#148; in the
Company&#146;s Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K for the fiscal
year ended January&nbsp;28, 2000.
